    47	impl SsaFormingVisitor<'_> {
    48	    /// Consume this expression and assign it to a variable (unless it's already an Identifier).
    49	    pub fn consume_expression_and_define(&mut self, input: Expression) -> (Expression, Vec<Statement>) {
    50	        let (expr, mut statements) = self.consume_expression(input);
    51	        if matches!(expr, Expression::Path(..) | Expression::Unit(..) | Expression::Err(..)) {
    52	            (expr, statements)
    53	        } else {
    54	            let (place, statement) = self.unique_simple_definition(expr);
    55	            statements.push(statement);
    56	            (Path::from(place).to_local().into(), statements)
    57	        }
    58	    }
    59	}
    60	
    61	impl ExpressionConsumer for SsaFormingVisitor<'_> {
    62	    type Output = (Expression, Vec<Statement>);
    63	
    64	    fn consume_array_access(&mut self, input: ArrayAccess) -> Self::Output {
    65	        let (array, statements) = self.consume_expression_and_define(input.array);
    66	        (ArrayAccess { array, ..input }.into(), statements)
    67	    }
    68	
    69	    fn consume_member_access(&mut self, input: MemberAccess) -> Self::Output {
    70	        // If the access expression is of the form `self.<name>`, then don't rename it.
    71	        if let Expression::Path(path) = &input.inner
    72	            && path.identifier().name == sym::SelfLower
    73	        {
    74	            return (input.into(), Vec::new());
    75	        }
    76	
    77	        let (inner, statements) = self.consume_expression_and_define(input.inner);
    78	        (MemberAccess { inner, ..input }.into(), statements)
    79	    }
    80	
    81	    fn consume_tuple_access(&mut self, input: TupleAccess) -> Self::Output {
    82	        let (tuple, statements) = self.consume_expression_and_define(input.tuple);
    83	        (TupleAccess { tuple, ..input }.into(), statements)
    84	    }
    85	
    86	    /// Consumes an array expression, accumulating any statements that are generated.
    87	    fn consume_array(&mut self, input: ArrayExpression) -> Self::Output {
    88	        let mut statements = Vec::new();
    89	
    90	        // Process the elements, accumulating any statements produced.
    91	        let elements = input
    92	            .elements
    93	            .into_iter()
    94	            .map(|element| {
    95	                let (element, mut stmts) = self.consume_expression_and_define(element);
    96	                statements.append(&mut stmts);
    97	                element
    98	            })
    99	            .collect();
   100	
   101	        (ArrayExpression { elements, ..input }.into(), statements)
   102	    }
   103	
   104	    /// Consumes a binary expression, accumulating any statements that are generated.
   105	    fn consume_binary(&mut self, input: BinaryExpression) -> Self::Output {
   106	        // Reconstruct the lhs of the binary expression.
   107	        let (left, mut statements) = self.consume_expression_and_define(input.left);
   108	        // Reconstruct the rhs of the binary expression.
   109	        let (right, mut right_statements) = self.consume_expression_and_define(input.right);
   110	        // Accumulate any statements produced.
   111	        statements.append(&mut right_statements);
   112	
   113	        (BinaryExpression { left, right, ..input }.into(), statements)
   114	    }
   115	
   116	    /// Consumes a call expression without visiting the function name, accumulating any statements that are generated.
   117	    fn consume_call(&mut self, input: CallExpression) -> Self::Output {
   118	        let mut statements = Vec::new();
   119	
   120	        // Process the arguments, accumulating any statements produced.
   121	        let arguments = input
   122	            .arguments
   123	            .into_iter()
   124	            .map(|argument| {
   125	                let (argument, mut stmts) = self.consume_expression_and_define(argument);
   126	                statements.append(&mut stmts);
   127	                argument
   128	            })
   129	            .collect();
   130	
   131	        (
   132	            CallExpression {
   133	                // Note that we do not rename the function name.
   134	                arguments,
   135	                ..input
   136	            }
   137	            .into(),
   138	            statements,
   139	        )
   140	    }
   141	
   142	    fn consume_dynamic_call(&mut self, input: DynamicCallExpression) -> Self::Output {
   143	        let mut statements = Vec::new();
   144	
   145	        let (target, mut target_stmts) = self.consume_expression_and_define(input.target_program);
   146	        statements.append(&mut target_stmts);
   147	
   148	        let network = input.network.map(|n| {
   149	            let (n, mut stmts) = self.consume_expression_and_define(n);
   150	            statements.append(&mut stmts);
   151	            n
   152	        });
   153	
   154	        let arguments = input
   155	            .arguments
   156	            .into_iter()
   157	            .map(|argument| {
   158	                let (argument, mut stmts) = self.consume_expression_and_define(argument);
   159	                statements.append(&mut stmts);
   160	                argument
   161	            })
   162	            .collect();
   163	
   164	        (DynamicCallExpression { target_program: target, network, arguments, ..input }.into(), statements)
   165	    }
   166	
   167	    /// Consumes a cast expression, accumulating any statements that are generated.
   168	    fn consume_cast(&mut self, input: CastExpression) -> Self::Output {
   169	        // Reconstruct the expression being casted.
   170	        let (expression, statements) = self.consume_expression_and_define(input.expression);
   171	        (CastExpression { expression, ..input }.into(), statements)
   172	    }
   173	
   174	    /// Consumes a composite initialization expression with renamed variables, accumulating any statements that are generated.
   175	    fn consume_composite_init(&mut self, input: CompositeExpression) -> Self::Output {
   176	        let mut statements = Vec::new();
   177	
   178	        // Process the members, accumulating any statements produced.
   179	        let members: Vec<CompositeFieldInitializer> = input
   180	            .members
   181	            .into_iter()
   182	            .map(|arg| {
   183	                let (expression, mut stmts) = if let Some(expr) = arg.expression {
   184	                    self.consume_expression_and_define(expr)
   185	                } else {
   186	                    self.consume_path(Path::from(arg.identifier).to_local())
   187	                };
   188	                // Accumulate any statements produced.
   189	                statements.append(&mut stmts);
   190	
   191	                // Return the new member.
   192	                CompositeFieldInitializer { expression: Some(expression), ..arg }
   193	            })
   194	            .collect();
   195	
   196	        // Reorder the members to match that of the composite definition.
   197	
   198	        // Lookup the composite definition.
   199	        let composite_location = input.path.expect_global_location();
   200	        let composite_definition: &Composite = self
   201	            .state
   202	            .symbol_table
   203	            .lookup_record(self.program, composite_location)
   204	            .or_else(|| self.state.symbol_table.lookup_struct(self.program, composite_location))
   205	            .expect("Type checking guarantees this definition exists.");
   206	
   207	        // Initialize the list of reordered members.
   208	        let mut reordered_members = Vec::with_capacity(members.len());
   209	
   210	        // Collect the members of the init expression into a map.
   211	        let mut member_map: IndexMap<Symbol, CompositeFieldInitializer> =
   212	            members.into_iter().map(|member| (member.identifier.name, member)).collect();
   213	
   214	        // If we are initializing a record, add the `owner` first.
   215	        // Note that type checking guarantees that the above fields exist.
   216	        if composite_definition.is_record {
   217	            // Add the `owner` field.
   218	            // Note that the `unwrap` is safe, since type checking guarantees that the member exists.
   219	            reordered_members.push(member_map.shift_remove(&sym::owner).unwrap());
   220	        }
   221	
   222	        // For each member of the composite definition, push the corresponding member of the init expression.
   223	        for member in &composite_definition.members {
   224	            // If the member is part of a record and it is `owner` then we have already added it.
   225	            if !(composite_definition.is_record && matches!(member.identifier.name, sym::owner)) {
   226	                // Lookup and push the member of the init expression.
   227	                // Note that the `unwrap` is safe, since type checking guarantees that the member exists.
   228	                reordered_members.push(member_map.shift_remove(&member.identifier.name).unwrap());
   229	            }
   230	        }
   231	
   232	        (CompositeExpression { members: reordered_members, ..input }.into(), statements)
   233	    }
   234	
   235	    /// Retrieve the new name for this `Identifier`.
   236	    ///
   237	    /// Note that this shouldn't be used for `Identifier`s on the lhs of definitions or
   238	    /// assignments.
   239	    fn consume_path(&mut self, path: Path) -> Self::Output {
   240	        if let Some(name) = path.try_local_symbol() {
   241	            // If lookup fails, then we didn't rename it.
   242	            let name = *self.rename_table.lookup(name).unwrap_or(&name);
   243	            (path.with_updated_last_symbol(name).into(), Default::default())
   244	        } else {
   245	            (path.into(), Default::default())
   246	        }
   247	    }
   248	
   249	    /// Consumes and returns the literal without making any modifications.
   250	    fn consume_literal(&mut self, input: Literal) -> Self::Output {
   251	        (input.into(), Default::default())
   252	    }
   253	
   254	    fn consume_repeat(&mut self, input: RepeatExpression) -> Self::Output {
   255	        let (expr, statements) = self.consume_expression_and_define(input.expr);
   256	
   257	        // By now, the repeat count should be a literal. So we just ignore it. There is no need to SSA it.
   258	        (RepeatExpression { expr, ..input }.into(), statements)
   259	    }
   260	
   261	    /// Consumes a ternary expression, accumulating any statements that are generated.
   262	    fn consume_ternary(&mut self, input: TernaryExpression) -> Self::Output {
   263	        // Reconstruct the condition of the ternary expression.
   264	        let (cond_expr, mut statements) = self.consume_expression_and_define(input.condition);
   265	        // Reconstruct the if-true case of the ternary expression.
   266	        let (if_true_expr, if_true_statements) = self.consume_expression_and_define(input.if_true);
   267	        // Reconstruct the if-false case of the ternary expression.
   268	        let (if_false_expr, if_false_statements) = self.consume_expression_and_define(input.if_false);
   269	
   270	        // Accumulate any statements produced.
   271	        statements.extend(if_true_statements);
   272	        statements.extend(if_false_statements);
   273	
   274	        (
   275	            TernaryExpression { condition: cond_expr, if_true: if_true_expr, if_false: if_false_expr, ..input }.into(),
   276	            statements,
   277	        )
   278	    }
   279	
   280	    /// Consumes a tuple expression, accumulating any statements that are generated
   281	    fn consume_tuple(&mut self, input: TupleExpression) -> Self::Output {
   282	        let mut statements = Vec::new();
   283	
   284	        // Process the elements, accumulating any statements produced.
   285	        let elements = input
   286	            .elements
   287	            .into_iter()
   288	            .map(|element| {
   289	                let (element, mut stmts) = self.consume_expression_and_define(element);
   290	                statements.append(&mut stmts);
   291	                element
   292	            })
   293	            .collect();
   294	
   295	        (TupleExpression { elements, ..input }.into(), statements)
   296	    }
   297	
   298	    /// Consumes a unary expression, accumulating any statements that are generated.
   299	    fn consume_unary(&mut self, input: UnaryExpression) -> Self::Output {
   300	        // Reconstruct the operand of the unary expression.
   301	        let (receiver, statements) = self.consume_expression_and_define(input.receiver);
   302	        (UnaryExpression { receiver, ..input }.into(), statements)
   303	    }
   304	
   305	    fn consume_unit(&mut self, input: UnitExpression) -> Self::Output {
   306	        (input.into(), Default::default())
   307	    }
   308	
   309	    fn consume_intrinsic(&mut self, input: leo_ast::IntrinsicExpression) -> Self::Output {
   310	        let mut statements = Vec::new();
   311	        let expr = IntrinsicExpression {
   312	            arguments: input
   313	                .arguments
   314	                .into_iter()
   315	                .map(|arg| {
   316	                    let (arg, mut stmts) = self.consume_expression_and_define(arg);
   317	                    statements.append(&mut stmts);
   318	                    arg
   319	                })
   320	                .collect(),
   321	            ..input
   322	        }
   323	        .into();
   324	
   325	        (expr, statements)
   326	    }
   327	
   328	    fn consume_async(&mut self, input: leo_ast::AsyncExpression) -> Self::Output {
   329	        (input.into(), Default::default())
   330	    }
   331	}

    41	use leo_span::Symbol;

    44	
    45	impl StatementConsumer for SsaFormingVisitor<'_> {
    46	    type Output = Vec<Statement>;
    47	
    48	    /// Consumes the expressions in an `AssertStatement`, returning the list of simplified statements.
    49	    fn consume_assert(&mut self, input: AssertStatement) -> Self::Output {
    50	        let (variant, mut statements) = match input.variant {
    51	            AssertVariant::Assert(expr) => {
    52	                let (expr, statements) = self.consume_expression_and_define(expr);
    53	                (AssertVariant::Assert(expr), statements)
    54	            }
    55	            AssertVariant::AssertEq(left, right) => {
    56	                // Reconstruct the lhs of the binary expression.
    57	                let (left, mut statements) = self.consume_expression_and_define(left);
    58	                // Reconstruct the rhs of the binary expression.
    59	                let (right, right_statements) = self.consume_expression_and_define(right);
    60	                // Accumulate any statements produced.
    61	                statements.extend(right_statements);
    62	
    63	                (AssertVariant::AssertEq(left, right), statements)
    64	            }
    65	            AssertVariant::AssertNeq(left, right) => {
    66	                // Reconstruct the lhs of the binary expression.
    67	                let (left, mut statements) = self.consume_expression_and_define(left);
    68	                // Reconstruct the rhs of the binary expression.
    69	                let (right, right_statements) = self.consume_expression_and_define(right);
    70	                // Accumulate any statements produced.
    71	                statements.extend(right_statements);
    72	
    73	                (AssertVariant::AssertNeq(left, right), statements)
    74	            }
    75	        };
    76	
    77	        // Add the assert statement to the list of produced statements.
    78	        statements.push(AssertStatement { variant, ..input }.into());
    79	
    80	        statements
    81	    }
    82	
    83	    /// Consume all `AssignStatement`s, renaming as necessary.
    84	    fn consume_assign(&mut self, mut assign: AssignStatement) -> Self::Output {
    85	        let (value, mut statements) = self.consume_expression(assign.value);
    86	        if let Expression::Path(path) = assign.place {
    87	            // Then assign a new unique name to the left-hand-side of the assignment.
    88	            // Note that this order is necessary to ensure that the right-hand-side uses the correct name when consuming a complex assignment.
    89	            // We really expect `path` to refer to a local variable so we only care about the result of `identifier().name`.
    90	            let new_place = self.rename_identifier(*path.identifier());
    91	
    92	            statements.push(self.simple_definition(new_place, value));
    93	            statements
    94	        } else {
    95	            // It must be a sequence of accesses ending in an identifier.
    96	            // This loop will iterate until the identifier is reached.
    97	            // For example, `some_identifier[i].member` -> `some_identifier[i]` -> `some_identifier`.
    98	            // All we need to do is consume that identifier to possibly get a new name.
    99	            let mut place = &mut assign.place;
   100	            loop {
   101	                match place {
   102	                    Expression::ArrayAccess(array_access) => place = &mut array_access.array,
   103	                    Expression::MemberAccess(member_access) => place = &mut member_access.inner,
   104	                    Expression::TupleAccess(tuple_access) => place = &mut tuple_access.tuple,
   105	                    expr @ Expression::Path(..) => {
   106	                        let (new_expr, statements2) = self.consume_expression(std::mem::take(expr));
   107	                        *expr = new_expr;
   108	                        statements.extend(statements2);
   109	                        assign.value = value;
   110	                        statements.push(assign.into());
   111	                        return statements;
   112	                    }
   113	                    _ => panic!("Type checking should have ensured this is not possible."),
   114	                }
   115	            }
   116	        }
   117	    }
   118	
   119	    /// Consumes a `Block`, flattening its constituent `ConditionalStatement`s.
   120	    fn consume_block(&mut self, block: Block) -> Self::Output {
   121	        block.statements.into_iter().flat_map(|statement| self.consume_statement(statement)).collect()
   122	    }
   123	
   124	    /// Consumes a `ConditionalStatement`, producing phi functions (assign statements) for variables written in the then-block and otherwise-block.
   125	    /// For more information on phi functions, see https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Static_single_assignment_form.
   126	    /// Furthermore a new `AssignStatement` is introduced for non-trivial expressions in the condition of `ConditionalStatement`s.
   127	    /// For example,
   128	    ///   - `if x > 0 { x = x + 1 }` becomes `let $cond$0 = x > 0; if $cond$0 { x = x + 1; }`
   129	    ///   - `if true { x = x + 1 }` remains the same.
   130	    ///   - `if b { x = x + 1 }` remains the same.
   131	    fn consume_conditional(&mut self, conditional: ConditionalStatement) -> Self::Output {
   132	        // Simplify the condition and add it into the rename table.
   133	        let (condition, mut statements) = self.consume_expression_and_define(conditional.condition);
   134	
   135	        // Instantiate a `RenameTable` for the then-block.
   136	        self.push();
   137	
   138	        // Consume the then-block.
   139	        let then = Block {
   140	            span: conditional.then.span,
   141	            id: conditional.then.id,
   142	            statements: self.consume_block(conditional.then),
   143	        };
   144	
   145	        // Remove the `RenameTable` for the then-block.
   146	        let if_table = self.pop();
   147	
   148	        // Instantiate a `RenameTable` for the otherwise-block.
   149	        self.push();
   150	
   151	        // Consume the otherwise-block and flatten its constituent statements into the current block.
   152	        let otherwise = conditional.otherwise.map(|otherwise| Box::new(Statement::Block(match *otherwise {
   153	            Statement::Block(block) => Block {
   154	                span: block.span,
   155	                id: block.id,
   156	                statements: self.consume_block(block),
   157	            },
   158	            Statement::Conditional(conditional) => Block {
   159	                span: conditional.span,
   160	                id: conditional.id,
   161	                statements: self.consume_conditional(conditional),
   162	            },
   163	            _ => panic!("Type checking guarantees that the otherwise-block of a conditional statement is a block or another conditional statement."),
   164	        })));
   165	
   166	        // Remove the `RenameTable` for the otherwise-block.
   167	        let else_table = self.pop();
   168	
   169	        // Add reconstructed conditional statement to the list of produced statements.
   170	        statements.push(ConditionalStatement { condition: condition.clone(), then, otherwise, ..conditional }.into());
   171	
   172	        // Compute the write set for the variables written in the then-block or otherwise-block.
   173	        let if_write_set: IndexSet<&Symbol> = IndexSet::from_iter(if_table.local_names());
   174	        let else_write_set: IndexSet<&Symbol> = IndexSet::from_iter(else_table.local_names());
   175	        let write_set = if_write_set.union(&else_write_set);
   176	
   177	        // For each variable in the write set, instantiate and add a phi function to the list of produced statements.
   178	        for symbol in write_set {
   179	            // Note that phi functions only need to be instantiated if the variable exists before the `ConditionalStatement`.
   180	            if self.rename_table.lookup(**symbol).is_some() {
   181	                // Helper to lookup an and create an argument for the phi function.
   182	                let create_phi_argument = |table: &RenameTable, symbol: Symbol| -> Expression {
   183	                    let name =
   184	                        *table.lookup(symbol).unwrap_or_else(|| panic!("Symbol {symbol} should exist in the program."));
   185	                    let id = *table
   186	                        .lookup_id(&name)
   187	                        .unwrap_or_else(|| panic!("Symbol {name} should exist in the rename table."));
   188	                    Path::from(Identifier { name, span: Default::default(), id }).to_local().into()
   189	                };
   190	
   191	                // Create a new name for the variable written to in the `ConditionalStatement`.
   192	                let new_name = self.state.assigner.unique_symbol(symbol, "$");
   193	
   194	                // Create the arguments for the phi function.
   195	                let if_true = create_phi_argument(&if_table, **symbol);
   196	                let if_false = create_phi_argument(&else_table, **symbol);
   197	
   198	                // Create a new node ID for the phi function.
   199	                let id = self.state.node_builder.next_id();
   200	                // Update the type of the node ID.
   201	                let Some(type_) = self.state.type_table.get(&if_true.id()) else {
   202	                    panic!("Type checking guarantees that all expressions have a type.");
   203	                };
   204	                self.state.type_table.insert(id, type_);
   205	
   206	                // Construct a ternary expression for the phi function.
   207	                let (value, stmts) = self.consume_ternary(TernaryExpression {
   208	                    condition: condition.clone(),
   209	                    if_true,
   210	                    if_false,
   211	                    span: Default::default(),
   212	                    id,
   213	                });
   214	
   215	                statements.extend(stmts);
   216	
   217	                // Get the ID for the new name of the variable.
   218	                let id = *self.rename_table.lookup_id(symbol).unwrap_or_else(|| {
   219	                    panic!("The ID for the symbol `{symbol}` should already exist in the rename table.")
   220	                });
   221	
   222	                // Update the `RenameTable` with the new name of the variable.
   223	                self.rename_table.update(**symbol, new_name, id);
   224	
   225	                // Create a new `DefinitionStatement` for the phi function.
   226	                let identifier = Identifier { name: new_name, span: Default::default(), id };
   227	                let assignment = self.simple_definition(identifier, value);
   228	
   229	                // Store the generated phi function.
   230	                statements.push(assignment);
   231	            }
   232	        }
   233	
   234	        statements
   235	    }
   236	
   237	    fn consume_const(&mut self, _: ConstDeclaration) -> Self::Output {
   238	        // Constants have been propagated everywhere by this point, so we no longer need const declarations.
   239	        Default::default()
   240	    }
   241	
   242	    /// Consumes the `DefinitionStatement` into an `AssignStatement`, renaming the left-hand-side as appropriate.
   243	    fn consume_definition(&mut self, definition: DefinitionStatement) -> Self::Output {
   244	        match definition.place {
   245	            DefinitionPlace::Single(identifier) => {
   246	                // Consume the right-hand-side of the definition.
   247	                let (value, mut rhs_statements) = self.consume_expression(definition.value);
   248	
   249	                // Rename identifier if needed.
   250	                let new_identifier = if self.rename_defs { self.rename_identifier(identifier) } else { identifier };
   251	
   252	                // Create a new assignment statement.
   253	                rhs_statements.push(self.simple_definition(new_identifier, value));
   254	                rhs_statements
   255	            }
   256	            DefinitionPlace::Multiple(identifiers) => {
   257	                // Rename identifiers if needed.
   258	                let new_identifiers = if self.rename_defs {
   259	                    identifiers.into_iter().map(|id| self.rename_identifier(id)).collect()
   260	                } else {
   261	                    identifiers
   262	                };
   263	
   264	                // We don't need to update the type table, as the new identifiers have
   265	                // the same IDs as the old ones.
   266	
   267	                // Construct the lhs of the assignment.
   268	                let place = DefinitionPlace::Multiple(new_identifiers);
   269	
   270	                let (value, mut rhs_statements) = self.consume_expression(definition.value);
   271	
   272	                // Create the definition.
   273	                let def_stmt = DefinitionStatement { place, type_: None, value, ..definition }.into();
   274	                rhs_statements.push(def_stmt);
   275	                rhs_statements
   276	            }
   277	        }
   278	    }
   279	
   280	    /// Consumes the expressions associated with `ExpressionStatement`, returning the simplified `ExpressionStatement`.
   281	    fn consume_expression_statement(&mut self, mut input: ExpressionStatement) -> Self::Output {
   282	        let (expr, mut statements) = self.consume_expression(input.expression);
   283	        input.expression = expr;
   284	        statements.push(input.into());
   285	        statements
   286	    }
   287	
   288	    fn consume_iteration(&mut self, _input: IterationStatement) -> Self::Output {
   289	        panic!("`IterationStatement`s should not be in the AST at this phase of compilation.");
   290	    }
   291	
   292	    /// Reconstructs the expression associated with the return statement, returning a simplified `ReturnStatement`.
   293	    /// Note that type checking guarantees that there is at most one `ReturnStatement` in a block.
   294	    fn consume_return(&mut self, mut input: ReturnStatement) -> Self::Output {
   295	        if let Expression::Tuple(tuple_expr) = &mut input.expression {
   296	            // Leave tuple expressions alone.
   297	            let mut statements = Vec::new();
   298	            for element in tuple_expr.elements.iter_mut() {
   299	                let (new_element, new_statements) = self.consume_expression_and_define(std::mem::take(element));
   300	                *element = new_element;
   301	                statements.extend(new_statements);
   302	            }
   303	            statements.push(input.into());
   304	            statements
   305	        } else {
   306	            let (expression, mut statements) = self.consume_expression_and_define(input.expression);
   307	            input.expression = expression;
   308	            statements.push(input.into());
   309	            statements
   310	        }
   311	    }
   312	}
   313

   123	    fn visit_value(&mut self, input: &Literal) -> AleoExpr {
   124	        // AVM can only parse decimal numbers.
   125	        let literal = if let LiteralVariant::Unsuffixed(value) = &input.variant {
   126	            // For unsuffixed lierals, consult the `type_table` for their types. The type checker
   127	            // ensures that their type can only be `Integer`, `Field`, `Group`, or `Scalar`.
   128	            match self.state.type_table.get(&input.id) {
   129	                Some(Type::Integer(int_ty)) => Literal {
   130	                    variant: LiteralVariant::Integer(int_ty, value.clone()),
   131	                    id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
   132	                    span: input.span,
   133	                },
   134	                Some(Type::Field) => Literal {
   135	                    variant: LiteralVariant::Field(value.clone()),
   136	                    id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
   137	                    span: input.span,
   138	                },
   139	                Some(Type::Group) => Literal {
   140	                    variant: LiteralVariant::Group(value.clone()),
   141	                    id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
   142	                    span: input.span,
   143	                },
   144	                Some(Type::Scalar) => Literal {
   145	                    variant: LiteralVariant::Scalar(value.clone()),
   146	                    id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
   147	                    span: input.span,
   148	                },
   149	                _ => panic!(
   150	                    "Unexpected type for unsuffixed integer literal. This should have been caught by the type checker"
   151	                ),
   152	            }
   153	        } else {
   154	            input.clone()
   155	        };
   156	
   157	        fn prepare_literal(s: &str) -> String {
   158	            // If there's a `-`, separate it from the rest of the string.
   159	            let (neg, rest) = s.strip_prefix("-").map(|rest| ("-", rest)).unwrap_or(("", s));
   160	            // Remove leading zeros.
   161	            let mut rest = rest.trim_start_matches('0');
   162	            if rest.is_empty() {
   163	                rest = "0";
   164	            }
   165	            format!("{neg}{rest}")
   166	        }
   167	
   168	        match literal.variant.clone() {
   169	            LiteralVariant::Identifier(val) => AleoExpr::Identifier(val),
   170	            LiteralVariant::Address(val) => AleoExpr::Address(prepare_literal(&val)),
   171	            LiteralVariant::Boolean(val) => AleoExpr::Bool(val),
   172	            LiteralVariant::Field(val) => AleoExpr::Field(prepare_literal(&val)),
   173	            LiteralVariant::Group(val) => AleoExpr::Group(prepare_literal(&val)),
   174	            LiteralVariant::Integer(itype, val) => {
   175	                let val = val.replace('_', "");
   176	
   177	                match itype {
   178	                    IntegerType::U8 => AleoExpr::U8(u8::from_str_by_radix(&val).unwrap()),
   179	                    IntegerType::U16 => AleoExpr::U16(u16::from_str_by_radix(&val).unwrap()),
   180	                    IntegerType::U32 => AleoExpr::U32(u32::from_str_by_radix(&val).unwrap()),
   181	                    IntegerType::U64 => AleoExpr::U64(u64::from_str_by_radix(&val).unwrap()),
   182	                    IntegerType::U128 => AleoExpr::U128(u128::from_str_by_radix(&val).unwrap()),
   183	                    IntegerType::I8 => AleoExpr::I8(i8::from_str_by_radix(&val).unwrap()),
   184	                    IntegerType::I16 => AleoExpr::I16(i16::from_str_by_radix(&val).unwrap()),
   185	                    IntegerType::I32 => AleoExpr::I32(i32::from_str_by_radix(&val).unwrap()),
   186	                    IntegerType::I64 => AleoExpr::I64(i64::from_str_by_radix(&val).unwrap()),
   187	                    IntegerType::I128 => AleoExpr::I128(i128::from_str_by_radix(&val).unwrap()),
   188	                }
   189	            }
   190	            LiteralVariant::Scalar(val) => AleoExpr::Scalar(prepare_literal(&val)),
   191	            LiteralVariant::Signature(val) => AleoExpr::Signature(prepare_literal(&val)),
   192	            LiteralVariant::String(val) => AleoExpr::String(val),
   193	            LiteralVariant::None | LiteralVariant::Unsuffixed(..) => {
   194	                panic!("This literal variant should no longer exist at code generation")
   195	            }
   196	        }
   197	    }

The `literal_to_value` function at line 61 returns `Ok(value)` even for unsuffixed literals because it calls `resolve_if_unsuffixed` which can return the original (unsuffixed) value if `expected_ty` is `None`. So the check passes even if `type_info` is `None`.

So the question is: when do we have an unsuffixed literal without type information? This could happen if something in the compiler pipeline creates a new literal node without populating the type table.

So when `to_expression` is called on an `Unsuffixed` value, it creates an unsuffixed literal. Then `value_to_expression` in `visitor.rs` copies the type information recursively. But for an unsuffixed literal, the type would be some concrete type (e.g., `u128`), so `copy_types_recursively` would set the type of the unsuffixed literal to that concrete type. That should be fine.

But wait, what if `value_to_expression` returns `None`? Let me check:

```rust
pub fn value_to_expression(&mut self, value: &Value, span: Span, id: NodeID) -> Option<(Expression, NodeID)> {
    let ty = self.state.type_table.get(&id)?.clone();
    ...
    let new_expr = value.to_expression(span, &self.state.node_builder, &ty, &struct_lookup)?;
    ...
}
```

If `type_table.get(&id)` returns `None`, then `value_to_expression` returns `None`. But in `reconstruct_literal`, the call is:

```rust
let (new_expr, _) = self.value_to_expression(&constant_value, span, id).expect(VALUE_ERROR);
```

where `VALUE_ERROR = "A non-future value should always be able to be converted into an expression"`.

So `value_to_expression` would fail if the type is not in the type table. But that would be a different panic.

Let me look at the actual flow more carefully. In `reconstruct_literal`:

1. It gets `type_info` from the type table for the input literal.
2. It calls `const_eval::literal_to_value(&input, &type_info)`.
3. If that succeeds, and if the variant is `Unsuffixed`, it does `type_info.expect(...)`.

Now, if `type_info` is `None`, `literal_to_value` is called with `None`. For an unsuffixed literal, this calls `resolve_if_unsuffixed(None, ...)` which returns `Ok(self.clone())` (the unsuffixed value). So it succeeds and returns `Ok(value)`.

Then we check if variant is `Unsuffixed`. It is. Then we call `type_info.expect(...)` which panics.

So the fix should be: if `type_info` is `None`, we should not try to resolve the unsuffixed literal. We should just keep it as is.

But actually, looking at the non-SSA version (`const_propagation/ast.rs`), it has the same issue. Both need to be fixed.

Wait, but the PR description says the issue is with arrays as mapping keys. How does that cause unsuffixed literals without type info?

Let me think about this differently. Maybe the issue is not about unsuffixed literals at all - maybe the panic occurs because the type table lookup returns `None` for some other reason, and the literal happens to be unsuffixed.

Let me look at how array keys in mappings work. An array key in a mapping like `[address;2]` would mean that `Mapping::get` or `Mapping::set` takes an array as a key. Let me look at how this gets transformed during compilation.

Let me look at the `StorageLowering` pass which handles mapping operations:

    17	use super::StorageLoweringVisitor;
    18	
    19	use leo_ast::*;
    20	use leo_span::{Span, Symbol, sym};
    21	
    22	impl leo_ast::AstReconstructor for StorageLoweringVisitor<'_> {
    23	    type AdditionalInput = ();
    24	    type AdditionalOutput = Vec<Statement>;
    25	
    26	    /* Types */
    27	    fn reconstruct_array_type(&mut self, input: ArrayType) -> (Type, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
    28	        let (length, stmts) = self.reconstruct_expression(*input.length, &());
    29	        (
    30	            Type::Array(ArrayType {
    31	                element_type: Box::new(self.reconstruct_type(*input.element_type).0),
    32	                length: Box::new(length),
    33	            }),
    34	            stmts,
    35	        )
    36	    }
    37	
    38	    fn reconstruct_composite_type(&mut self, input: CompositeType) -> (Type, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
    39	        let mut statements = Vec::new();
    40	
    41	        let const_arguments = input
    42	            .const_arguments
    43	            .into_iter()
    44	            .map(|arg| {
    45	                let (expr, stmts) = self.reconstruct_expression(arg, &Default::default());
    46	                statements.extend(stmts);
    47	                expr
    48	            })
    49	            .collect();
    50	
    51	        (Type::Composite(CompositeType { const_arguments, ..input }), statements)
    52	    }
    53	
    54	    /* Expressions */
    55	    fn reconstruct_array_access(
    56	        &mut self,
    57	        mut input: ArrayAccess,
    58	        _additional: &(),
    59	    ) -> (Expression, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
    60	        let (array, mut stmts_array) = self.reconstruct_expression(input.array, &());
    61	        let (index, mut stmts_index) = self.reconstruct_expression(input.index, &());
    62	
    63	        input.array = array;
    64	        input.index = index;
    65	
    66	        // Merge side effects
    67	        stmts_array.append(&mut stmts_index);
    68	
    69	        (input.into(), stmts_array)
    70	    }
    71	
    72	    fn reconstruct_intrinsic(
    73	        &mut self,
    74	        mut input: IntrinsicExpression,
    75	        _additional: &Self::AdditionalInput,
    76	    ) -> (Expression, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
    77	        match Intrinsic::from_symbol(input.name, &input.type_parameters) {
    78	            Some(Intrinsic::VectorPush) => {
    79	                // Unpack arguments
    80	                let [vector_expr, value_expr] = &mut input.arguments[..] else {
    81	                    panic!("Vector::push should have 2 arguments");
    82	                };
    83	
    84	                // Validate vector type
    85	                assert!(matches!(self.state.type_table.get(&vector_expr.id()), Some(Type::Vector(_))));
    86	                let Expression::Path(path_to_vector) = vector_expr else {
    87	                    panic!("Vector::push can only be called with `Expression::Path`");
    88	                };
    89	
    90	                let (value, stmts) = self.reconstruct_expression(value_expr.clone(), &());
    91	
    92	                // Input:
    93	                //   Vector::push(v, 42u32)
    94	                //
    95	                // Lowered reconstruction:
    96	                //   let $len_var = Mapping::get_or_use(len_map, false, 0u32);
    97	                //   Mapping::set(vec_map, $len_var, 42u32);
    98	                //   Mapping::set(len_map, false, $len_var + 1);
    99	
   100	                // Reconstruct value
   101	                let (vec_path_expr, len_path_expr) = self.generate_vector_mapping_exprs(path_to_vector);
   102	
   103	                // let $len_var = Mapping::get_or_use(len_map, false, 0u32)
   104	                let len_var_sym = self.state.assigner.unique_symbol("$len_var", "$");
   105	                let len_var_ident =
   106	                    Identifier { name: len_var_sym, span: Default::default(), id: self.state.node_builder.next_id() };
   107	                let get_len_expr = self.get_vector_len_expr(len_path_expr.clone(), input.span);
   108	                let len_stmt = self.state.assigner.simple_definition(
   109	                    len_var_ident,
   110	                    get_len_expr,
   111	                    self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
   112	                );
   113	                let len_var_expr: Expression = len_var_ident.into();
   114	
   115	                // index + 1
   116	                let literal_one = self.literal_one_u32();
   117	                let increment_expr = self.binary_expr(len_var_expr.clone(), BinaryOperation::Add, literal_one);
   118	
   119	                // Mapping::set(vec__, $len_var, value)
   120	                let set_vec_stmt_expr = self.set_mapping_expr(vec_path_expr, len_var_expr.clone(), value, input.span);
   121	
   122	                // Mapping::set(len_map, false, $len_var + 1)
   123	                let literal_false = self.literal_false();
   124	                let set_len_stmt = Statement::Expression(ExpressionStatement {
   125	                    expression: self.set_mapping_expr(len_path_expr, literal_false, increment_expr, input.span),

   127	                    id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
   128	                });
   129	
   130	                (set_vec_stmt_expr, [stmts, vec![len_stmt, set_len_stmt]].concat())

   132	
   133	            Some(Intrinsic::VectorLen) => {
   134	                // Input:
   135	                //   Vector::len(v)
   136	                //
   137	                // Lowered reconstruction:

   149	                };

   152

   154	                (get_len_expr, vec![])
   155	            }
   156	
   157	            Some(Intrinsic::VectorPop) => {

   171	
   172	                // Input:
   173	                //   Vector::pop(v)
   174	                //
   175	                // Lowered reconstruction:

   178	                //   $len_var > 0 ? Mapping::get_or_use(vec_map, $len_var - 1, zero_value) : None
   179	                let (vec_path_expr, len_path_expr) = self.generate_vector_mapping_exprs(path_to_vector);
   180	
   181	                // let $len_var = Mapping::get_or_use(len_map, false, 0u32)

   189	                    self.state.node_builder.next_id(),

   191	                let len_var_expr: Expression = len_var_ident.into();
   192	
   193	                // $len_var > 0
   194	                let literal_zero = self.literal_zero_u32();
   195	                let len_gt_zero_expr = self.binary_expr(len_var_expr.clone(), BinaryOperation::Gt, literal_zero);
   196	
   197	                // $len_var - 1
   198	                let literal_one = self.literal_one_u32();
   199	                let len_minus_one_expr =
   200	                    self.binary_expr(len_var_expr.clone(), BinaryOperation::SubWrapped, literal_one);
   201	
   202	                // ternary for new length: ($len_var > 0 ? $len_var - 1 : $len_var)
   203	                let new_len_expr = self.ternary_expr(
   204	                    len_gt_zero_expr.clone(),
   205	                    len_minus_one_expr.clone(),
   206	                    len_var_expr.clone(),
   207	                    input.span,
   208	                );
   209	
   210	                // Mapping::set(len_map, false, new_len)
   211	                let literal_false = self.literal_false();
   212	                let set_len_stmt = Statement::Expression(ExpressionStatement {

   215	                    id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
   216	                });
   217	
   218	                // zero value for element type (used as default in get_or_use)
   219	                let zero = self.zero(&element_type);
   220

   222	                let get_or_use_expr =

   224	
   225	                // ternary: $len_var > 0 ? get(vec, len-1) : None
   226	                let none_expr: Expression = Literal::none(Span::default(), self.state.node_builder.next_id()).into();
   227	                let ternary_expr = self.ternary_expr(len_gt_zero_expr, get_or_use_expr, none_expr, input.span);
   228	
   229	                (ternary_expr, vec![len_stmt, set_len_stmt])
   230	            }
   231	
   232	            Some(Intrinsic::VectorGet) => {
   233	                // Unpack arguments (container, index/key)
   234	                let [vector_expr, key_expr] = &mut input.arguments[..] else {

   261	                // let $len_var = Mapping::get_or_use(len_map, false, 0u32)
   262	                let len_var_sym = self.state.assigner.unique_symbol("$len_var", "$");

   273	                // index < len

    24	pub struct StorageLoweringVisitor<'a> {
    25	    pub state: &'a mut CompilerState,
    26	    // The name of the current program scope
    27	    pub program: Symbol,
    28	    pub new_mappings: IndexMap<Location, Mapping>,
    29	}
    30	
    31	impl StorageLoweringVisitor<'_> {
    32	    /// Returns the two mapping expressions that back a vector: `<base>__` (values)
    33	    /// and `<base>__len__` (length).
    34	    ///
    35	    /// Panics if `expr` is not a `Path`.
    36	    pub fn generate_vector_mapping_exprs(&mut self, path: &Path) -> (Expression, Expression) {
    37	        let base = path.identifier().name;
    38	        let val = Symbol::intern(&format!("{base}__"));
    39	        let len = Symbol::intern(&format!("{base}__len__"));
    40	
    41	        let make_expr = |sym| {
    42	            let ident = Identifier::new(sym, self.state.node_builder.next_id());
    43	            let mut p = Path::from(ident);
    44	
    45	            if let Some(program) = path.user_program().filter(|p| p.as_symbol() != self.program) {
    46	                p = p.with_user_program(*program);
    47	            }
    48	
    49	            p.to_global(Location::new(self.program, vec![sym])).into()
    50	        };
    51	
    52	        (make_expr(val), make_expr(len))
    53	    }
    54	
    55	    /// Standard literal expressions used frequently
    56	    pub fn literal_false(&mut self) -> Expression {
    57	        Literal::boolean(false, Span::default(), self.state.node_builder.next_id()).into()
    58	    }
    59	
    60	    pub fn literal_zero_u32(&mut self) -> Expression {
    61	        Literal::integer(IntegerType::U32, "0".to_string(), Span::default(), self.state.node_builder.next_id()).into()
    62	    }
    63	
    64	    pub fn literal_one_u32(&mut self) -> Expression {
    65	        Literal::integer(IntegerType::U32, "1".to_string(), Span::default(), self.state.node_builder.next_id()).into()
    66	    }
    67	
    68	    /// Generates `_mapping_get_or_use(len_path_expr, false, 0u32)`
    69	    pub fn get_vector_len_expr(&mut self, len_path_expr: Expression, span: Span) -> Expression {
    70	        IntrinsicExpression {
    71	            name: sym::_mapping_get_or_use,
    72	            type_parameters: vec![],
    73	            input_types: vec![],
    74	            return_types: vec![],
    75	            arguments: vec![len_path_expr, self.literal_false(), self.literal_zero_u32()],
    76	            span,
    77	            id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
    78	        }
    79	        .into()
    80	    }
    81	
    82	    /// Generates `_mapping_set(path_expr, key_expr, value_expr)`

    84	        &mut self,

    86	        key_expr: Expression,
    87	        value_expr: Expression,
    88	        span: Span,
    89	    ) -> Expression {

    93	            input_types: vec![],
    94	            return_types: vec![],
    95	            arguments: vec![path_expr, key_expr, value_expr],
    96	            span,
    97	            id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
    98	        }
    99	        .into()
   100	    }

   103	    pub fn get_mapping_expr(&mut self, path_expr: Expression, key_expr: Expression, span: Span) -> Expression {
   104	        IntrinsicExpression {
   105	            name: sym::_mapping_get,
   106	            type_parameters: vec![],
   107	            input_types: vec![],
   108	            return_types: vec![],
   109	            arguments: vec![path_expr, key_expr],
   110	            span,
   111	            id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
   112	        }
   113	        .into()
   114	    }

   120	        key_expr: Expression,

   122	        span: Span,

   125	            name: sym::_mapping_get_or_use,
   126	            type_parameters: vec![],
   127	            input_types: vec![],
   128	            return_types: vec![],
   129	            arguments: vec![path_expr, key_expr, default_expr],
   130	            span,
   131	            id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
   132	        }
   133	        .into()
   134	    }
   135	
   136	    /// Generates a ternary expression
   137	    pub fn ternary_expr(
   138	        &mut self,
   139	        condition: Expression,
   140	        if_true: Expression,
   141	        if_false: Expression,
   142	        span: Span,
   143	    ) -> Expression {
   144	        TernaryExpression { condition, if_true, if_false, span, id: self.state.node_builder.next_id() }.into()
   145	    }
   146	
   147	    /// Generates a binary expression
   148	    pub fn binary_expr(&mut self, left: Expression, op: BinaryOperation, right: Expression) -> Expression {
   149	        BinaryExpression { op, left, right, span: Span::default(), id: self.state.node_builder.next_id() }.into()
   150	    }
   151	
   152	    /// Produces a zero expression for `Type` `ty`.
   153	    pub fn zero(&self, ty: &Type) -> Expression {
   154	        // zero value for element type (used as default in get_or_use)
   155	        let symbol_table = &self.state.symbol_table;
   156	        let struct_lookup = |loc: &Location| {
   157	            symbol_table
   158	                .lookup_struct(self.program, loc)
   159	                .unwrap()
   160	                .members
   161	                .iter()
   162	                .map(|mem| (mem.identifier.name, mem.type_.clone()))
   163	                .collect()
   164	        };
   165	        Expression::zero(ty, Span::default(), &self.state.node_builder, &struct_lookup)
   166	            .expect("zero value generation failed")
   167	    }
   168	
   169	    pub fn reconstruct_path_or_locator(&self, input: Expression) -> Expression {
   170	        let location = match input {
   171	            Expression::Path(ref path) if path.is_local() => {
   172	                // nothing to do for local paths.
   173	                return input;
   174	            }
   175	            Expression::Path(ref path) => {
   176	                // Otherwise, it should be a global path.
   177	                path.expect_global_location().clone()
   178	            }
   179	            _ => panic!("unexpected expression type"),
   180	        };
   181	
   182	        // Check if this path corresponds to a global symbol.
   183	        let Some(var) = self.state.symbol_table.lookup_global(self.program, &location) else {
   184	            // Nothing to do
   185	            return input;
   186	        };
   187	
   188	        match &var.type_ {
   189	            Some(Type::Mapping(_)) => {
   190	                // No transformation needed for mappings.
   191	                input
   192	            }
   193	
   194	            Some(Type::Optional(OptionalType { inner })) => {
   195	                // Input:
   196	                //   storage x: field;
   197	                //   ...
   198	                //   let y = x;
   199	                //
   200	                // Lowered reconstruction:
   201	                //  mapping x__: bool => field
   202	                //  let y = x__.contains(false)
   203	                //      ? x__.get_or_use(false, 0field)
   204	                //      : None;
   205	
   206	                let id = || self.state.node_builder.next_id();
   207	                let var_name = location.path.last().unwrap();
   208	
   209	                // Path to the mapping backing the optional variable: `<var_name>__`
   210	                let mapping_symbol = Symbol::intern(&format!("{var_name}__"));
   211	                let mapping_ident = Identifier::new(mapping_symbol, id());
   212	
   213	                // === Build expressions ===
   214	                let mapping_expr: Expression = {
   215	                    let path = if let Expression::Path(path) = input {
   216	                        path
   217	                    } else {
   218	                        panic!("unexpected expression type");
   219	                    };
   220	
   221	                    let mut base_path = Path::from(mapping_ident);
   222	
   223	                    // Attach user program only if it's present and different from current
   224	                    if let Some(user_program) = path.user_program()
   225	                        && user_program.as_symbol() != self.program
   226	                    {
   227	                        base_path = base_path.with_user_program(*user_program);
   228	                    }
   229	
   230	                    base_path.to_global(Location::new(self.program, vec![mapping_ident.name])).into()
   231	                };
   232	
   233	                let false_literal: Expression = Literal::boolean(false, Span::default(), id()).into();
   234	
   235	                // `<var_name>__.contains(false)`
   236	                let contains_expr: Expression = IntrinsicExpression {
   237	                    name: sym::_mapping_contains,
   238	                    type_parameters: vec![],
   239	                    input_types: vec![],
   240	                    return_types: vec![],
   241	                    arguments: vec![mapping_expr.clone(), false_literal.clone()],
   242	                    span: Span::default(),
   243	                    id: id(),
   244	                }
   245	                .into();
   246	
   247	                // zero value for element type
   248	                let zero = self.zero(inner);
   249	
   250	                // `<var_name>__.get_or_use(false, zero_value)`
   251	                let get_or_use_expr: Expression = IntrinsicExpression {
   252	                    name: sym::_mapping_get_or_use,
   253	                    type_parameters: vec![],
   254	                    input_types: vec![],
   255	                    return_types: vec![],
   256	                    arguments: vec![mapping_expr.clone(), false_literal, zero],
   257	                    span: Span::default(),
   258	                    id: id(),
   259	                }
   260	                .into();
   261	
   262	                // `None`
   263	                let none_expr =
   264	                    Expression::Literal(Literal { variant: LiteralVariant::None, span: Span::default(), id: id() });
   265	
   266	                // Combine into ternary:
   267	                // `<var_name>__.contains(false) ? <var_name>__.get_or_use(false, zero_val) : None`
   268	                let ternary_expr: Expression = TernaryExpression {
   269	                    condition: contains_expr,
   270	                    if_true: get_or_use_expr,
   271	                    if_false: none_expr,
   272	                    span: Span::default(),
   273	                    id: id(),
   274	                }
   275	                .into();
   276	
   277	                ternary_expr
   278	            }
   279	
   280	            _ => {
   281	                panic!("Expected an optional or a mapping, found {:?}", var.type_);
   282	            }
   283	        }
   284	    }
   285	}

    72	    fn reconstruct_intrinsic(
    73	        &mut self,
    74	        mut input: IntrinsicExpression,
    75	        _additional: &Self::AdditionalInput,
    76	    ) -> (Expression, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
    77	        match Intrinsic::from_symbol(input.name, &input.type_parameters) {
    78	            Some(Intrinsic::VectorPush) => {
    79	                // Unpack arguments
    80	                let [vector_expr, value_expr] = &mut input.arguments[..] else {
    81	                    panic!("Vector::push should have 2 arguments");
    82	                };
    83	
    84	                // Validate vector type
    85	                assert!(matches!(self.state.type_table.get(&vector_expr.id()), Some(Type::Vector(_))));
    86	                let Expression::Path(path_to_vector) = vector_expr else {
    87	                    panic!("Vector::push can only be called with `Expression::Path`");
    88	                };
    89	
    90	                let (value, stmts) = self.reconstruct_expression(value_expr.clone(), &());
    91	
    92	                // Input:
    93	                //   Vector::push(v, 42u32)
    94	                //
    95	                // Lowered reconstruction:
    96	                //   let $len_var = Mapping::get_or_use(len_map, false, 0u32);
    97	                //   Mapping::set(vec_map, $len_var, 42u32);
    98	                //   Mapping::set(len_map, false, $len_var + 1);
    99	
   100	                // Reconstruct value
   101	                let (vec_path_expr, len_path_expr) = self.generate_vector_mapping_exprs(path_to_vector);
   102	
   103	                // let $len_var = Mapping::get_or_use(len_map, false, 0u32)
   104	                let len_var_sym = self.state.assigner.unique_symbol("$len_var", "$");
   105	                let len_var_ident =
   106	                    Identifier { name: len_var_sym, span: Default::default(), id: self.state.node_builder.next_id() };
   107	                let get_len_expr = self.get_vector_len_expr(len_path_expr.clone(), input.span);
   108	                let len_stmt = self.state.assigner.simple_definition(
   109	                    len_var_ident,
   110	                    get_len_expr,
   111	                    self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
   112	                );
   113	                let len_var_expr: Expression = len_var_ident.into();
   114	
   115	                // index + 1
   116	                let literal_one = self.literal_one_u32();
   117	                let increment_expr = self.binary_expr(len_var_expr.clone(), BinaryOperation::Add, literal_one);
   118	
   119	                // Mapping::set(vec__, $len_var, value)
   120	                let set_vec_stmt_expr = self.set_mapping_expr(vec_path_expr, len_var_expr.clone(), value, input.span);
   121	
   122	                // Mapping::set(len_map, false, $len_var + 1)
   123	                let literal_false = self.literal_false();
   124	                let set_len_stmt = Statement::Expression(ExpressionStatement {
   125	                    expression: self.set_mapping_expr(len_path_expr, literal_false, increment_expr, input.span),
   126	                    span: input.span,
   127	                    id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
   128	                });
   129	
   130	                (set_vec_stmt_expr, [stmts, vec![len_stmt, set_len_stmt]].concat())
   131	            }
   132	
   133	            Some(Intrinsic::VectorLen) => {
   134	                // Input:
   135	                //   Vector::len(v)
   136	                //
   137	                // Lowered reconstruction:
   138	                //   Mapping::get_or_use(len_map, false, 0u32)
   139	
   140	                //  Unpack arguments
   141	                let [vector_expr] = &mut input.arguments[..] else {
   142	                    panic!("Vector::len should have 1 argument");
   143	                };
   144	
   145	                // Validate vector type
   146	                assert!(matches!(self.state.type_table.get(&vector_expr.id()), Some(Type::Vector(_))));
   147	                let Expression::Path(path_to_vector) = vector_expr else {
   148	                    panic!("Vector::len can only be called with `Expression::Path`");
   149	                };
   150	
   151	                let (_vec_path_expr, len_path_expr) = self.generate_vector_mapping_exprs(path_to_vector);
   152	
   153	                let get_len_expr = self.get_vector_len_expr(len_path_expr, input.span);
   154	                (get_len_expr, vec![])
   155	            }
   156	
   157	            Some(Intrinsic::VectorPop) => {
   158	                // Unpack argument
   159	                let [vector_expr] = &mut input.arguments[..] else {
   160	                    panic!("Vector::pop should have 1 argument");
   161	                };
   162	
   163	                // Validate vector type
   164	                let Some(Type::Vector(VectorType { element_type })) = self.state.type_table.get(&vector_expr.id())
   165	                else {
   166	                    panic!("argument to Vector::pop should be of type `Vector`.");
   167	                };
   168	                let Expression::Path(path_to_vector) = vector_expr else {
   169	                    panic!("Vector::pop can only be called with `Expression::Path`");
   170	                };

   172	                // Input:
   173	                //   Vector::pop(v)
   174	                //
   175	                // Lowered reconstruction:
   176	                //   let $len_var = Mapping::get_or_use(len_map, false, 0u32);
   177	                //   Mapping::set(len_map, false, $len_var > 0 ? $len_var - 1 : $len_var);
   178	                //   $len_var > 0 ? Mapping::get_or_use(vec_map, $len_var - 1, zero_value) : None
   179	                let (vec_path_expr, len_path_expr) = self.generate_vector_mapping_exprs(path_to_vector);
   180	
   181	                // let $len_var = Mapping::get_or_use(len_map, false, 0u32)

   187	                    len_var_ident,
   188	                    get_len_expr,
   189	                    self.state.node_builder.next_id(),
   190	                );

   192	
   193	                // $len_var > 0
   194	                let literal_zero = self.literal_zero_u32();
   195	                let len_gt_zero_expr = self.binary_expr(len_var_expr.clone(), BinaryOperation::Gt, literal_zero);
   196	
   197	                // $len_var - 1
   198	                let literal_one = self.literal_one_u32();
   199	                let len_minus_one_expr =
   200	                    self.binary_expr(len_var_expr.clone(), BinaryOperation::SubWrapped, literal_one);
   201	
   202	                // ternary for new length: ($len_var > 0 ? $len_var - 1 : $len_var)
   203	                let new_len_expr = self.ternary_expr(
   204	                    len_gt_zero_expr.clone(),
   205	                    len_minus_one_expr.clone(),
   206	                    len_var_expr.clone(),
   207	                    input.span,
   208	                );

   213	                    expression: self.set_mapping_expr(len_path_expr.clone(), literal_false, new_len_expr, input.span),
   214	                    span: input.span,
   215	                    id: self.state.node_builder.next_id(),

```rust
fn reconstruct_literal(&mut self, mut input: Literal, _additional: &()) -> (Expression, Self::AdditionalOutput) {
    let type_info = self.state.type_table.get(&input.id());

    // If this is an optional, then unwrap it first.
    let type_info = type_info.as_ref().map(|ty| match ty {
        Type::Optional(opt) => *opt.inner.clone(),
        _ => ty.clone(),
    });

    if let Ok(value) = const_eval::literal_to_value(&input, &type_info) {
        match input.variant {
            LiteralVariant::Address(ref s) if s.ends_with("aleo") => {
                // Do not fold program names as the VM needs to handle them directly
                (input.into(), None)
            }

            // If we know the type of an unsuffixed literal, might as well change it to a suffixed literal.
            LiteralVariant::Unsuffixed(s) => {
                match type_info.expect("Expected type information to be available") {
                    ...
                }
                (input.into(), Some(value))
            }
            _ => (input.into(), Some(value)),
        }
    } else {
        (input.into(), None)
    }
}
```

The fix should be straightforward: if `type_info` is `None` and the literal is `Unsuffixed`, we should not panic. Instead, we should just return the input as-is (similar to what happens when `literal_to_value` fails).

But wait, `literal_to_value` with `None` type_info actually succeeds for unsuffixed literals - it returns an unsuffixed Value. So the code enters the `Ok` branch, then checks if variant is `Unsuffixed`, and then panics because `type_info` is `None`.

The fix should be: if `type_info` is `None`, we should not try to resolve the unsuffixed literal. We should just keep it as-is. This matches the behavior of just returning `(input.into(), None)` for the case where we can't resolve the type.

All tests pass. Now let me think about edge cases:

1. **What if `type_info` is `None` for an unsuffixed literal?** - My fix handles this by simply not modifying the literal. The unsuffixed literal stays as-is, and later passes (like code generation) will need to handle it. But code generation also has a potential panic for unsuffixed literals without type info. However, if type info is missing, the code generation would also panic. But the type checker should have ensured all literals have types by that point.

2. **What about the `code_generation/expression.rs` case?** - I didn't fix that because by code generation time, all unsuffixed literals should have been resolved. But if there's a case where type info is missing at code generation, that's a different bug. Let me check if it also needs the same fix:

Actually, looking at the code generation case:
```rust
match self.state.type_table.get(&input.id) {
    Some(Type::Integer(int_ty)) => ...,
    Some(Type::Field) => ...,
    Some(Type::Group) => ...,
    Some(Type::Scalar) => ...,
    _ => panic!("Unexpected type for unsuffixed integer literal..."),
}
```

If `type_table.get` returns `None`, the `_` branch is taken, which panics. This could also be fixed, but it would hide a real problem (missing type info). The proper fix would be to keep the unsuffixed literal as-is when type is None, but that might cause issues in AVM. Let me leave it as-is for now since the PR description specifically mentions the SSA constant propagation panic.
